###begin article-title 0
###xml 25 50 25 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 25 50 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
Two conserved modules of Schizosaccharomyces pombe Mediator regulate distinct cellular pathways
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Present address: Tomas Linder, Department of Cellular and Molecular Pharmacology, University of California San Francisco, 1700 4th Street, PO Box 25430, Byers Hall 4308A, San Francisco, CA 94158-25430, USA
###end p 1
###begin p 2
Nina N. Rasmussen, Evolva A/S, Bulowsvej 25, DK-1870 Frederiksberg C, Denmark
###end p 2
###begin p 3
###xml 0 16 0 16 <!--CREATIVE COMMONS-->
CREATIVE COMMONSThis is an Open Access article distributed under the terms of the Creative Commons Attribution Non-Commercial License ( which permits unrestricted non-commercial use, distribution, and reproduction in any medium, provided the original work is properly cited.
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 138 163 138 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 372 380 372 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 427 435 427 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 526 527 526 527 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 521 527 521 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 557 559 557 559 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 566 568 566 568 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 553 592 553 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>ts</sup>, med17<sup>ts</sup>, &#916;med18, &#916;med20</italic>
###xml 597 607 589 595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med27</italic>
###xml 1097 1121 1085 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1218 1226 1206 1214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1231 1244 1219 1232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 138 163 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 372 380 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 427 435 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1097 1121 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1218 1226 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1231 1244 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
Mediator is an evolutionary conserved coregulator complex required for transcription of almost all RNA polymerase II-dependent genes. The Schizosaccharomyces pombe Mediator consists of two dissociable components-a core complex organized into a head and middle domain as well as the Cdk8 regulatory subcomplex. In this work we describe a functional characterization of the S. pombe Mediator. We report the identification of the S. pombe Med20 head subunit and the isolation of ts alleles of the core head subunit encoding med17+. Biochemical analysis of med8ts, med17ts, Deltamed18, Deltamed20 and Deltamed27 alleles revealed a stepwise head domain molecular architecture. Phenotypical analysis of Cdk8 and head module alleles including expression profiling classified the Mediator mutant alleles into one of two groups. Cdk8 module mutants flocculate due to overexpression of adhesive cell-surface proteins. Head domain-associated mutants display a hyphal growth phenotype due to defective expression of factors required for cell separation regulated by transcription factor Ace2. Comparison with Saccharomyces cerevisiae Mediator expression data reveals that these functionally distinct modules are conserved between S. pombe and S. cerevisiae.
###end p 4
###begin title 5
INTRODUCTION
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 171 172 171 172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 325 333 325 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 488 489 488 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 490 491 490 491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 319 324 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The Mediator is a multiprotein coregulator complex that is required for the transcription of almost all RNA polymerase II (pol II)-dependent genes in fungi and metazoans (1). Mediator is thought to act as an interface between the general transcription machinery and sequence-specific transcriptional activators. A pure yeast in vitro transcription system consisting of pol II and all the general transcription factors (GTFs) cannot be stimulated by activators in the absence of Mediator (2,3).
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 36 60 36 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 133 134 133 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 135 136 135 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 137 138 137 138 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 256 259 256 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6 B7 B8">6&#8211;8</xref>
###xml 36 60 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
Mediator was originally purified in Saccharomyces cerevisiae and has since then been isolated from several other eukaryotic species (1,4,5). These biochemical data revealed a core set of Mediator subunits that are conserved in most, if not all eukaryotes (6-8).
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 72 97 72 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 99 100 99 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 101 102 101 102 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 109 117 109 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 417 421 417 421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9 B10 B11">9&#8211;11</xref>
###xml 72 97 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 109 117 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
We have previously isolated and characterized the Mediator complex from Schizosaccharomyces pombe (6,9). The S. pombe Mediator exists in at least three states: a smaller core Mediator complex (S-Mediator) consisting of 15 subunits, a larger form (L-Mediator) consisting of core Mediator bound to a four-subunit module known as the Cdk8 module, and finally as a holoenzyme form with the core Mediator bound to pol II (9-11).
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 24 37 24 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 42 50 42 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 159 161 159 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 162 164 162 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 172 185 172 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 190 198 190 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 285 293 285 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 351 353 351 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 354 356 354 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 418 435 418 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro S. pombe</italic>
###xml 545 547 545 547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 631 633 631 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 634 636 634 636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 24 37 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 42 50 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 172 185 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 190 198 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 427 435 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
The Cdk8 module in both S. cerevisiae and S. pombe consists of four proteins: Med12 and Med13 as well as the cyclin-dependent kinase Cdk8 and its cyclin CycC (10,12). Both S. cerevisiae and S. pombe Cdk8 are able to phosphorylate the C-terminal domain of the largest subunit of pol II in vitro, which is thought to inhibit transcriptional initiation (10,13). Titration of the Cdk8 module-containing L-Mediator into an in vitro S. pombe transcription system has been shown to counteract the stimulatory effect of Mediator on basal transcription (14). Yet there is also evidence of a positive role for the Cdk8 module in activation (15,16).
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 43 56 43 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 159 161 159 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 162 164 162 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 207 215 207 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 307 309 307 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 357 370 357 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 409 417 409 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 481 489 481 489 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 43 56 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 207 215 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 357 370 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 409 417 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 481 489 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Electron microscopy (EM) studies of single S. cerevisiae core Mediator particles identified three distinct domains that have been named head, middle and tail (17,18). A similar investigation showed that the S. pombe core Mediator also contained a head and a middle domain, but lacked a visible tail domain (11). In agreement with this, only one of the five S. cerevisiae tail subunits, Med15, is conserved in S. pombe. So far Med15 has not been identified as a stable component of S. pombe Mediator.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 17 30 17 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 36 44 36 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 142 147 142 147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19 B20 B21 B22 B23">19&#8211;23</xref>
###xml 174 187 174 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 236 241 236 241 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20 B21 B22 B23 B24 B25">20&#8211;25</xref>
###xml 281 289 281 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 17 30 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 36 44 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 174 187 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 281 289 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Based on work in S. cerevisiae, the S. pombe middle domain is suggested to consist of Med1, Med4, Med7, Med10, Med14, Med19, Med21 and Med31 (19-23). The architecture of the S. cerevisiae head domain has been extensively characterized (20-25). From these data, we predict that the S. pombe head domain consists of Med8, Med17, Med18 and Med22 as well as the proposed Med20 subunit, which has not been identified as a stable Mediator component prior to this work.
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 106 114 106 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 227 240 227 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 601 609 601 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 106 114 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 227 240 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 601 609 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Here, we describe a structural and functional characterization of a representative set of subunits of the S. pombe Mediator. We identify the nonessential set of subunits in the head domain including a new subunit homologous to S. cerevisiae Med20. We report the isolation and characterization of conditional alleles of the essential head domain component Med17 and discuss its role in head domain architecture. Phenotypical analysis in combination with expression profiling of a representative set of Mediator mutant alleles allowed us to define two distinct functional classes of subunits within the S. pombe Mediator complex. Finally, the role of these separate classes of Mediator subunits in specific cellular pathways is discussed.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
MATERIAL AND METHODS
###end title 13
###begin title 14
###xml 0 25 0 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 0 25 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
Schizosaccharomyces pombe strains
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 51 58 51 58 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 60 85 60 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>

###xml 188 189 188 189 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

###xml 819 820 819 820 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 827 828 827 828 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 814 828 814 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med18<sup>+</sup>, med20<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 838 839 838 839 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 833 839 833 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med27<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 904 905 904 905 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 900 905 900 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ura4<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 944 946 944 946 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 959 961 959 961 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 977 979 977 979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>

###xml 4 9 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 60 85 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 1382 1387 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
All yeast strains used in this study are listed in Table 1. Schizosaccharomyces pombe cells were transformed by the lithium acetate procedure (26). Null mutants of med15+, med18+ and med20+ for expression profiling were generated using the kanMX selectable marker in the haploid h- strain MP9 as described (6) using the primers listed in . The double null mutant of med18+ and med20+ was constructed by crossing and tetrad analysis of the diploid TP396/TP235. Null mutants of med18+, med20+ and med27+ for protein purification were generated with the ura4+ gene as a selectable marker in an Ura- background. A plasmid containing the wild-type ura4+ gene (GenBank accession number X13976), pURA4, was constructed by inserting it into HindIII-digested pBluescript II SK (Stratagene). Segments of 500-bp flanking the med18+, med20+ and med27+ genes were PCR amplified and inserted on either side of the ura4+ marker to generate the plasmids pURA4-spmed18, pURA4-spmed20 and pURA4-spmed27, respectively. The knockout fragments were released from the respective plasmids by digesting with PvuII and transformed into the diploid strain TP219/TP220 carrying a Tandem Affinity Purification (TAP) tag on both copies of the med7+ gene. The obtained Ura+ diploids were sporulated and Ura+/G418-resistant spores were recovered, to generate strains TP416, TP417 and TP306, respectively. bSpore obtained after mating and sporulation of the diploid.

###begin title 19
###xml 18 20 18 20 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 13 20 13 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>ts</sup></italic>
Isolation of med17ts mutants
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 26 28 26 28 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 68 70 68 70 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 63 70 63 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>ts</sup></italic>
###xml 84 88 84 88 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 143 144 143 144 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 138 144 138 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 191 192 191 192 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 186 192 186 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 247 248 247 248 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 242 248 242 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 313 314 313 314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 309 314 309 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ura4<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 336 338 336 338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 339 341 339 341 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 400 401 400 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 395 401 395 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 506 508 506 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 603 604 601 602 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 785 801 777 793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 834 835 822 823 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 823 835 811 823 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17::ura4<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 954 955 942 943 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1177 1181 1159 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 785 801 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 1225 1230 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
A marker switch approach (27) was used for the construction of med17ts mutants. The LEU2 gene was inserted in a PacI site at 159 bp 3' of med17+ ORF in strain MP1 to generate TP384. The med17+ gene from position 429 bp 5' to 212 bp 3' of the med17+ ORF was cloned in pBluescript SK +/- and the 1.8-kb HindIII ura4+ fragment of pREP42X (28,29) was inserted into the PacI site at 159 bp 3' of the med17+ ORF to generate plasmid pTK1276. Mutagenesis of pTK1276 plasmid DNA was carried out with hydroxylamine (29) as follows: 10 mug of plasmid DNA was added to 500 mul ice-cold hydroxylamine solution (1 M H2NO.HCL, adjusted to pH 7 with NaOH) and incubated at 75degreesC for 90 min. Reactions were stopped by adding 200 mM NaCl, DNA was collected by EtOH precipitation and transformed in Escherichia coli strain DH5alpha. The med17::ura4+ fragment was exerted from a pool of mutagenized pTK1276 DNA with ApaLI and PacI and transformed into strain TP384. Ura+ transformants were selected on AA-Ura plates and replica-plated onto YES plates. After 3 days of incubation at 37degreesC, candidate colonies of temperature-sensitive (ts) mutants were isolated and tested for loss of the LEU2 gene on AA-Leu plates. Screening of 10 000 yeast transformants for a ts phenotype at 37degreesC yielded four independent mutant strains with a ts phenotype at 37degreesC on YES plates.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
###xml 20 32 20 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
Construction of the med17Delta50 allele
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 70 71 70 71 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 65 71 65 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 220 221 216 217 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 202 221 202 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50::ura4<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 326 327 322 323 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 423 424 419 420 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 428 429 424 425 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 428 429 424 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 493 494 483 484 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 499 500 489 490 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 489 513 479 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ura4<sup>+</sup> leu2<sup>&#8722;</sup> med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 551 552 537 538 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 547 552 533 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ura4<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 579 591 565 573 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 662 663 644 645 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 658 663 640 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ura4<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 699 700 681 682 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 694 700 676 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
One hundred and fifty nucleotides from position 1601-1751 of the med17+ ORF was deleted from plasmid pTK1276 introducing a NheI site 3' of the stop codon in the process to generate plasmid pTK1439. The med17Delta50::ura4+ sequence was exerted from pTK1439 with ApaLI and PacI and transformed into diploid strain TP384/MP2. Ura+ transformants were selected on AA-Ura plates and sporulated on MSA plates. After dissection Ura+/Leu- spores were tested for a ts phenotype at 37degreesC and an ura4+ leu2- med17Delta50 spore called TP390 isolated. The ura4+ gene was removed from the med17Delta50 strain TP390 by transforming with an 812-bp fragment spanning the ura4+ gene but not running into the med17+ ORF followed by selection on 5-FOA plates giving strain TP392.
###end p 22
###begin title 23
###xml 19 20 19 20 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 15 20 15 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med7<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 38 50 38 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 83 85 79 81 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 69 85 65 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sep15-598/med8<sup>ts</sup></italic>
TAP-tagging of med7+ in strain TP390 (med17Delta50) and strain MP10 (sep15-598/med8ts)
###end title 23
###begin p 24
###xml 31 32 31 32 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 27 32 27 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med7<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 101 103 101 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 109 111 109 111 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 159 178 159 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50 strain</italic>
###xml 203 205 199 201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 189 205 185 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sep15-598/med8<sup>ts</sup></italic>
The C-terminal part of the med7+ gene fused to a TAP-tag was exerted from plasmid pFA6a-kanMX6-CTAP2-spmed7 (10) with AvrII and EcoRV and transformed into the med17Delta50 strain TP392 and sep15-598/med8ts strain MP10 giving strains TP315 and TP308, respectively. Correct integration of constructs in the genome was verified by PCR analysis. The MP10 strain was a kind gift from M. Sipiczki (University of Debrecen, Hungary). In all cases, tetrad analysis and/or Southern blot analysis were/was applied to demonstrate that only one copy of the construct had integrated in the genome.
###end p 24
###begin title 25
###xml 0 24 0 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 0 24 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
Saccharomyces cerevisiae strains
###end title 25
###begin p 26
###xml 4 17 4 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 92 97 92 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MED20</italic>
###xml 102 107 102 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MED18</italic>
###xml 202 212 202 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 227 237 223 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 305 329 297 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 334 338 326 330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MED8</italic>
###xml 653 656 645 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TAP</italic>
###xml 657 661 649 653 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MED8</italic>
###xml 670 672 662 664 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 4 17 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 305 329 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
All S. cerevisiae deletion strains were purchased from Euroscarf. Deletion cassettes of the MED20 and MED18 genes were generated by amplifying the kanMX cassette from Euroscarf deletion strains BY0661 (Deltamed20) and BY04734 (Deltamed18) with 500-bp flanking sequence on either side of the kanMX marker. Saccharomyces cerevisiae TAP-MED8 cells were transformed with the amplified deletion cassettes using the lithium acetate procedure. Correct genomic integration was assayed by PCR using primers positioned at the very 5' end of either the upstream or coding region and conversely outside the 3' flanking regions of the transformation constructs. The TAP-MED8 strain (12) was a kind gift from Roger Kornberg (Stanford University, CA, USA).
###end p 26
###begin title 27
Protein purification
###end title 27
###begin p 28
###xml 59 83 53 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 175 178 169 172 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 192 200 186 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 226 229 220 223 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 684 685 672 673 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1594 1596 1570 1572 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 1597 1599 1573 1575 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 2386 2387 2344 2345 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 2389 2390 2347 2348 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 2500 2508 2458 2466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 59 83 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
###xml 123 128 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 192 200 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 241 246 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 286 291 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 426 431 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 2110 2128 <span type="species:ncbi:12227">tobacco etch virus</span>
###xml 2130 2133 <span type="species:ncbi:12227?0.9375">TEV</span>
###xml 2172 2175 <span type="species:ncbi:12227?0.9375">TEV</span>
###xml 2500 2508 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Cells were grown at 30degreesC unless otherwise specified. Saccharomyces cerevisiae cells were grown in YPD medium (10 g/l yeast extract, 20 g/l peptone, 20 g/l glucose) to OD600 3.5-4.0, and S. pombe cells were cultured to OD600 2.0-2.5 in yeast extract supplement (YES) medium (5 g/l yeast extract, 2 g/l casamino acids, 20 g/l glucose) supplemented with 0.2 g/l adenine. For preparation of whole-cell extract, we collected yeast cells from a 10 l culture by centrifugation (Beckman Instruments JLA-10 500 rotor, 9500 r.p.m., 10 min, 4degreesC), which were washed once with ice-cold water and suspended in 0.5 ml of 3 x lysis buffer (200 mM HEPES-KOH, pH 7.8, 15 mM KCl, 1.5 mM MgCl2, 0.5 mM EDTA, 15% glycerol, 0.5 mM dithiothreitol and protease inhibitors) per gram of cell pellet. For all purifications, we used a 100 x stock of protease inhibitors containing 100 mM phenylmethylsulfonyl fluoride, 200 mM pepstatin, 60 mM leupeptin and 200 mM benzamidine in 95% ethanol. Cells were lyzed by bead beating (Bead-Beater, Stratech, London, UK) for 25 cycles, with each cycle consisting of 30 s of beating and 90 s of rest. We cleared the supernatant by centrifugation (Beckman Instruments JLA-10 500 rotor at 9500 r.p.m., for 10 min, at 4degreesC), added 1/9 vol of 2 M KCl and stirred for 15 min. Polyethyleneimine was added to a final concentration of 0.02% followed by 15 min of stirring. Insoluble material was removed by ultracentrifugation (Beckman Instruments Ti45 rotor, 42 000 r.p.m., 30 min, 4degreesC). Mediator was purified according to the original TAP-tag purification protocol (30,31) with the following modifications. Nine hundred microliters of IgG-Sepharose (GE Healthcare) was added to 200 ml of extract and incubated for 2 h at 4degreesC. The IgG-Sepharose was collected by centrifugation (Beckman Instruments JA-17 rotor, 800 r.p.m., 1 min, 4degreesC), loaded onto a Poly-Prep column (Bio-Rad) and washed with 100 ml of IgG wash buffer (20 mM HEPES-NaOH, pH 7.5, 150 mM NaCl, 0.1% IGEPAL CA-630). Mediator was eluted in two steps: first, by incubation for 2 h at 16degreesC with 200 U of tobacco etch virus (TEV) NIa protease (Invitrogen) in 2 ml of TEV buffer (10 mM HEPES-NaOH, pH 7.5, 150 mM NaCl, 0.5 mM EDTA, 0.1% IGEPAL CA-630, 1 mM dithiothreitol), designated IgG eluate 1, and second, by elution of the IgG-Sepharose by incubation with 8 M urea, 100 mM NaH2PO4, 10 mM Tris-HCl, pH 7.7, for 5 min at room temperature, designated IgG eluate 2. For further purification of S. pombe Mediator, 500 microl of IgG eluate 1 was loaded onto a 1-ml heparin HiTrap column (GE Healthcare). The column was washed with 5 ml of buffer A-0.1 (20 mM HEPES-NaOH, pH 7.5, 10% glycerol, 0.5 mM EDTA, 1 mM dithiothreitol, protease inhibitors and the molarity of sodium chloride indicated after the hyphen) and then developed with a linear gradient (12 ml) of A-0.1 to A-1.2.
###end p 28
###begin title 29
Immunoblotting and production of antibodies
###end title 29
###begin p 30
###xml 30 31 30 31 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 16 31 16 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe med20<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 194 201 194 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 564 572 564 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 653 654 653 654 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 655 656 655 656 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 657 659 657 659 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 686 694 686 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 808 833 808 833 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 941 954 941 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1084 1097 1084 1097 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 16 24 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 194 206 <span type="species:ncbi:511693">E. coli BL21</span>
###xml 417 424 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbits</span>
###xml 564 572 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 686 694 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 808 833 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 941 954 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1084 1097 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
The full-length S. pombe med20+ coding region (GenBank accession NM_001019159) was inserted into the expression plasmid pGEX3X (GE Healthcare). The GST-Med20 fusion-protein was overexpressed in E. coli BL21 (DE3) pLysS cells (Stratagene) and subsequently purified using glutathione-Sepharose 4B (GE Healthcare) according to the recommendations of the manufacturer. The purified GST-Med20 protein was used to immunize rabbits. The antisera used in this study were taken 10 days after the second booster injection (AgriSera, Vannas, Sweden). Antibodies specific for S. pombe Mediator subunits Med17, Med18, Med27 and Med31 have been described previously (6,9,32). Antibodies specific for S. pombe CycC will be described in a parallel publication (Baraznenok,V. and Gustafsson,C.M., submitted for publication). Schizosaccharomyces pombe TAP-Med7 was detected with the soluble peroxidase anti-peroxidase complex (Sigma). Antibodies specific for S. cerevisiae Mediator subunits Med1, Med2, Med8 and Med11 were kind gifts from Stefan Bjorklund (Umea University, Sweden). Antibodies against S. cerevisiae Med18 and Med20 were kind gifts from R.A. Young (Whitehead Institute for Biomedical Research, Cambridge, MA, USA).
###end p 30
###begin title 31
Affymetrix GeneChip probe array hybridization
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 0 25 0 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 85 86 79 80 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 96 97 90 91 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 136 148 130 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 202 203 186 187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 213 214 197 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 433 435 405 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 681 683 653 655 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 1339 1342 1311 1314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mut</sup>
###xml 1335 1378 1307 1338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdk8<sup>mut</sup>, &#916;med12, &#916;med15, &#916;med18</italic>
###xml 1383 1393 1343 1349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 1459 1471 1415 1423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 1774 1775 1726 1727 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1770 1775 1722 1727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">atp1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 2251 2252 2203 2204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 0 25 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 365 370 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 485 490 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Schizosaccharomyces pombe strains were grown in EMM medium at 30degreesC until 5 x 106 to 1 x 107 cells/ml. Heat-stressed wild-type and med17Delta50 cells were cultured in EMM at 30degreesC until 5 x 106 to 1 x 107 cells/ml, spun down briefly and then resuspended in media pre-warmed to 37degreesC. Cells were harvested after 2 h of incubation at 37degreesC. Total yeast RNA was isolated using a hot acid phenol extraction protocol (33). Labeling and array hybridization to Affymetrix Yeast Genome 2.0 arrays were performed at the Karolinska Institute Affymetrix core facility (Huddinge, Sweden). Labeling and hybridization protocols are described in the Affymetrix users' manual (34). Washing and staining of arrays were performed using the GeneChip Fluidics Station 450. Arrays were scanned with the Affymetrix GeneArray scanner 3000 7G. Acquisition and quantification of array images as well as primary data analysis including normalization was performed using Affymetrix GeneChip Operating Software (GCOS). Data were processed with the MAS5 algorithm (scaling: all probe sets with target signal 100, normalization: user defined with normalization value 1). The expression profiling was done on two sets of samples. The first set contained transcript level data from three wild-type (MP9) cultures and three cultures of each of the cdk8mut, Deltamed12, Deltamed15, Deltamed18 and Deltamed20 strains. The second set contained transcript level data from two med17Delta50 mutant cultures and two corresponding wild-type (MP1) cultures. To rule out the possibility of global changes to the transcriptome in the Mediator mutants, all datasets were normalized to an internal housekeeping control mRNA. Through quantitative real-time PCR (see below) we established that the atp1+ gene displayed <1.5-fold change in all mutants when normalized to 28 S rRNA levels and was therefore chosen as the internal mRNA control. Within each set of samples the transcript signal intensities was compared to all the corresponding wild-type baseline controls, generating a total of nine comparisons for each mutant in the first series. The Affymetrix change-call algorithm designated every transcript in each individual comparison as increased, decreased or invariant (P-value threshold 0.0025) with reference to the wild-type baseline intensity. An average ratio change was calculated for each transcript in each strain by first adjusting the ratio change to one of all comparisons designated invariant and then calculating the geometric mean for the total number of comparisons. The normalized and filtered dataset is available as  in the online version of this article.
###end p 32

Hierarchical clustering was carried out with the TIGR Multiexperiment Viewer version 3.0.3 (35). ###begin title 35
Quantitative real-time PCR
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 154 157 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>
Total RNA was isolated as described above. RNA quality and concentration was determined using a BioAnalyser 2100 (Agilent). cDNA was synthesized with the AMV 1st Strand Synthesis Kit (Roche) using random hexamers. Relative quantification of cDNA was carried out in triplicate on a LightCycler 2.0 (Roche) using SYBR green technology and the FastStart DNA Master SYBR Green 1 mix (Roche). Standard curves were generated by at least four 5-fold serial dilutions of a single control sample and values within the linear exponential phase were used to calculate relative concentrations after normalization. Primers used for quantitative PCR are listed in .
###end p 36
###begin title 37
Northern blotting
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 52 54 52 54 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 137 139 130 132 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 266 268 258 260 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">18</sub>
###xml 379 380 370 371 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 424 426 410 412 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 455 484 <span type="species:ncbi:11801">Moloney murine leukemia virus</span>
Northern blotting was done as previously described (39) using 2 mug of heat-denatured total RNA (65degreesC for 3 min) in each lane. The 32P-labeled poly(dT) probe was obtained by reverse transcription: a 10 mul reaction containing 50 ng poly(rA), 100 pmol oligo(dT)18 primer, 1 mul 10 x M-MuLV reverse transcriptase reaction buffer [50 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8,3), 75 mM KCl, 3 mM MgCl2, 10 mM DTT], 100 pmol dTTP, 10 muCi [alpha-32P] dTTP (400 Ci/mmol), 100 U Moloney murine leukemia virus (M-MuLV) reverse transcriptase (NEBiolabs) was carried out at 37degreesC for 1 h. The poly(rA) template was removed by RNase H treatment where after RNase H was heat inactivated.
###end p 38

###xml 1404 1412 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Mass spectrometric analysis of partially purified S. pombe Mediator identified the hypothetical protein SPAC17G8.05 (GenBank accession NP_593728) as a potential Mediator subunit with an apparent mass of around 20 kDa (data not shown). SPAC17G8.05 has previously been predicted to be the S. pombe homolog of S. cerevisiae and mammalian Med20 (7). To demonstrate its stable Mediator association, S. pombe Mediator was purified with TAP-tag on the Med8 subunit and resolved by Heparin-Sepharose chromatography. Western analysis showed co-elution of Med20 with Med17 and Med27 (Figure 1A). Thus, Med20 is a stable subunit of S. pombe Mediator. Figure 1.Structural organization of the S. pombe Mediator head domain. (A) Schizosaccharomyces pombe TAP-Med8 Mediator was eluted from IgG-Sepharose by TEV cleavage and further resolved over Heparin-Sepharose as described in 'Material and methods' section. Western analysis of different fractions. (B) Western analysis of S. cerevisiae Mediator purified through a TAP-tag on the Med8 subunit from wild-type, Deltamed20 and Deltamed18 cells. (C) Western analysis of S. pombe Mediator purified through a TAP-tag on the Med7 subunit from wild-type, Deltamed18 and Deltamed20 cells. (D) Western analysis of S. pombe Mediator purified through a TAP-tag on the Med7 subunit from wild-type, Deltamed27 and med8ts/sep15-598 cells. (E) Proposed subunit organization of the S. pombe head domain based on the results in (C) and (D).

###begin p 42
###xml 31 39 31 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 63 64 63 64 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 66 91 66 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 290 291 290 291 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>

(D) Western analysis of S. pombe Mediator purified through a TAP-tag on the Med7 subunit from wild-type, Deltamed27 and med8ts/sep15-598 cells. (E) Proposed subunit organization of the S. pombe head domain based on the results in (C) and (D).

###begin p 43
###xml 3 16 3 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 84 86 84 86 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 87 89 87 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 90 92 90 92 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 125 138 125 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>

###xml 183 191 179 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 304 314 300 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>

###xml 3 16 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 125 138 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
In S. cerevisiae, Med20 and Med18 form a distinct submodule within the head domain (24,25,40). Med20 is completely lost from S. cerevisiae Mediator isolated from a Deltamed18 strain (Figure 1B, right lane). However, we could still detect reduced amounts of Med18 associated with Mediator isolated from a Deltamed20 strain (Figure 1B, middle lane).

###begin p 44
###xml 25 33 25 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 70 83 70 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 124 134 124 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 138 148 134 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 231 232 223 224 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 226 232 218 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med18<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 242 243 234 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 237 243 229 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med20<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 270 278 262 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 290 303 282 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 319 329 311 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 334 353 322 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20 S. pombe</italic>
###xml 429 431 413 415 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 488 489 472 473 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 483 489 467 473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med18<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 498 499 482 483 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 493 499 477 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med20<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 544 552 528 536 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 609 628 593 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20 S. pombe</italic>
###xml 701 711 681 687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 806 816 782 788 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 821 831 793 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 921 934 889 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 964 965 932 933 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 959 965 927 933 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med27<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1071 1072 1033 1034 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 1117 1118 1075 1076 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1098 1118 1060 1076 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med27 TAP-med7<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1163 1171 1121 1129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1251 1261 1203 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med27</italic>
###xml 25 33 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 70 83 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 270 278 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 290 303 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 345 353 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 602 607 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 620 628 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 921 934 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
To establish whether the S. pombe head domain is organized as that of S. cerevisiae diploid strains heterozygous for either Deltamed18 or Deltamed20 were made. After tetrad analysis, viability segregated 4:0 showing that both med18+ and med20+ are nonessential genes in S. pombe like their S. cerevisiae homologs. Both Deltamed18 and Deltamed20 S. pombe cells have a slow growth phenotype and fail to sporulate (data not shown) (41). We purified Mediator from strains lacking either med18+ or med20+, respectively, utilizing a TAP-tag on Med7 (Figure 1C). In agreement with our observations in budding yeast, Deltamed20 S. pombe Mediator contained reduced amounts of the Med18 subunit, whereas mutant Deltamed18 Mediator completely lacked Med20 after purification over IgG-Sepharose. In addition, both the Deltamed18 and Deltamed20 mutant Mediator lacked the Med27 subunit. No homolog of Med27 has been identified in the S. cerevisiae Mediator. Cells lacking med27+ (systematic name SPAC17C9.05c) are viable without any apparent phenotype at 30degreesC (data not shown) (6). Mediator purified from Deltamed27 TAP-med7+ cells still contained both Med18 and Med20 (Figure 1D, middle lane) consistent with the wild-type growth phenotype at 30degreesC of Deltamed27 cells. This suggests that Med27 is located proximally to the Med18/Med20 dimer on the periphery of the head domain.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 61 70 61 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sep15-598</italic>
###xml 79 81 79 81 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 75 81 75 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>ts</sup></italic>
###xml 114 119 114 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42 B43 B44">42&#8211;44</xref>
###xml 122 147 122 147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 171 173 171 173 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 167 173 167 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>ts</sup></italic>
###xml 219 229 219 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 322 324 318 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 392 394 388 390 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 388 398 384 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>ts</sup> TAP</italic>
###xml 403 404 399 400 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 399 404 395 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med7<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 445 453 441 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 656 664 652 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 794 802 790 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 893 906 889 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 908 910 904 906 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 122 147 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 513 518 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 656 664 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 893 906 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
A ts allele of the essential head domain subunit Med8 called sep15-598 (or med8ts for clarity) has been isolated (42-44). Schizosaccharomyces pombe cells carrying the med8ts allele display a similar growth phenotype as Deltamed18 cells suggesting that this allele could affect subunit interactions within the head domain (42). Western blot analysis revealed that Mediator purified from a med8ts TAP-med7+ strain had lost Med18, Med20 and Med27 (Figure 1D, right lane). Furthermore, Med8 interacts with Med20 in a yeast two-hybrid interaction analysis (data not shown). Thus, our observations suggest a step-wise structural organization of the nonessential S. pombe head domain subunits where Med27 is found on the very exterior connected to Med20, which in turn contacts Med18 that binds Med8 (Figure 1E). This model is in agreement with recent structural data of a Med8-Med18-Med20 trimer in S. cerevisiae (40).
###end p 45
###begin title 46
###xml 34 48 34 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe med17</italic>
###xml 34 42 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Isolation and characterization of S. pombe med17 ts alleles
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 4 17 4 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 96 98 96 98 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 99 101 99 101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 102 104 102 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 186 188 186 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 189 191 189 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 211 230 211 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae MED17</italic>
###xml 238 246 238 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srb4-138</italic>
###xml 354 361 354 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 363 365 363 365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 366 368 366 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 380 381 380 381 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 375 381 375 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 408 416 408 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 418 419 418 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 451 456 451 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17</italic>
###xml 467 475 467 475 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 564 566 564 566 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 643 644 643 644 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 638 644 638 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 754 759 748 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17</italic>
###xml 829 830 823 824 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 824 830 818 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1093 1101 1087 1095 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">de facto</italic>
###xml 1230 1235 1224 1229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17</italic>
###xml 1243 1255 1237 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 1346 1348 1336 1338 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 1341 1348 1331 1338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17<sup>ts</sup></italic>
###xml 4 17 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 211 224 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 408 416 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 467 475 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 511 524 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">fission yeast</span>
The S. cerevisiae Med17 subunit is located in the head domain and essential for cell viability (20,24,45) reflecting its importance as a scaffold for the remaining head domain subunits (22,25). The ts allele of S. cerevisiae MED17 termed srb4-138 was instrumental in demonstrating the universal requirement for Mediator in pol II-dependent transcription in vivo (45,46). The med17+ gene is also essential in S. pombe (6). We constructed a conditional med17 allele in S. pombe to understand Mediator function in fission yeast. We employed a marker switch approach (27) to establish a ts allele by targeted hydroxylamine mutagenesis at the med17+ locus and isolated four independent mutant strains with a ts phenotype at 37degreesC on YES plates. All four med17 mutants had acquired base changes in the C-terminal part of the med17+ coding sequence resulting in premature stop codons within the last 50 C-terminal amino acids of the Med17 protein. We considered the possibility that low levels of read-through of the premature stop codon could still produce full-length Med17 protein and that a de facto C-terminal truncation would be lethal. Thus, we constructed a strain lacking the last 50 C-terminal amino acids and termed this med17 allele med17Delta50 allele, which has a ts phenotype indistinguishable from the four previously isolated med17ts alleles.
###end p 47

###xml 0 24 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
###xml 115 140 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 259 267 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 528 536 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 592 605 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 762 775 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 922 930 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1115 1123 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1997 2005 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Saccharomyces cerevisiae cells with the srb4-138 allele immediately stop growing after a shift to 37degreesC (45). Schizosaccharomyces pombe med17Delta50 cells displayed a slightly more gradual response when heat stressed. After shifting a mid log culture of S. pombe med17Delta50 cells growing at 30degreesC to 37degreesC an initial decrease of growth rate after 2.5 h was observed with growth ceasing altogether after 7.5 h (Figure 2A). The same pattern was obtained with the isolated med17ts alleles (data not shown). As the S. pombe med17Delta50 allele appeared subtly different from the S. cerevisiae srb4-138 allele, we isolated total RNA from med17Delta50 cells and wild-type controls cultured at 30degreesC as well as 2 h after a shift to 37degreesC. In S. cerevisiae srb4-138 cells, transcription ceases abruptly with most mRNA transcripts gone after 1 h (45). In contrast, northern blot analysis of heat-shocked S. pombe med17Delta50 cells show no detectable decrease in mRNA levels even after 9 h at 37degreesC (Figure 2B). Figure 2.Isolation and characterization of temperature-sensitive alleles of the S. pombe med17+ gene. (A) med17Delta50 cells and wild type (MP1) were grown to OD600 = 0.1 (106 cells/ml) in YES medium at 30degreesC. Cultures were then divided in two, spun down and resuspended in medium preheated to either 30degreesC or 37degreesC. Cell density was continually measured until growth of the med17Delta50 culture at 37degreesC had ceased. Due to septation defects in the med17Delta50 cells, samples were sonicated briefly prior to absorbance measurement. (B) Northern blot analysis of global mRNA levels in med17Delta50 cells following resuspension in medium preheated at either 30degreesC or 37degreesC. The upper panel shows a membrane probed with radioactively labeled poly-T as described in 'Material and Methods' section. Lower panel indicates rRNA loading control as observed in the ethidium bromide-stained agarose gel. (C) Western analysis of Tap-purified S. pombe Mediator from med17Delta50 TAP-med7+ cells grown at 30degreesC. (D) The same purification as in (C) but cells were cultured at 22degreesC.
###end p 48

###begin p 50
###xml 27 39 27 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 48 49 44 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 44 49 40 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med7<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 298 306 288 296 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 342 363 332 349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 392 414 378 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae srb4-138</italic>
###xml 512 514 498 500 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 561 573 547 555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 636 648 612 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 659 667 631 639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1178 1191 1150 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1202 1204 1174 1176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 1205 1207 1177 1179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 1262 1270 1234 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1304 1312 1276 1284 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 151 154 <span type="species:ncbi:12227?0.9375">TEV</span>
###xml 342 350 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 392 405 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 902 907 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1178 1191 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1262 1270 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Mediator was purified from med17Delta50 TAP-med7+ strain grown at 30degreesC in order to characterize its subunit composition. Western blotting of the TEV eluate revealed that the head module proteins Med17 and Med27 were completely lost while the amounts of Med18 and Med20 were severely reduced (Figure 2C). This drastic destabilization of S. pombe med17Delta50 Mediator was reminiscent of S. cerevisiae srb4-138 Mediator, which fractures at the head/middle domain boundary irrespective of growth temperature (19). We repeated the purification, culturing the med17Delta50 cells at 22degreesC and in this case Med17 was present in the med17Delta50 Mediator (Figure 2D). The head module subunit Med18 was still present whereas both Med20 and Med27 were lost from the mutant complex. This suggested that Med17 could be interacting with Med20 and Med27 independently of Med18. In support of this notion, yeast two-hybrid interaction analysis revealed that Med17 has physical contacts with Med20 and Med27 (data not shown). We have no two-hybrid data regarding interactions between Med17 and Med18. Direct interactions between Med17 and Med20 have also been reported previously in S. cerevisiae Mediator (22,24). Thus, we suggest the structural organization of the S. pombe head domain subunits depicted in Figure 1E with Med27 situated on the exterior connected to Med20, which contacts Med18 that ultimately binds Med8. Med17 could serve as a scaffold interacting with Med8, Med20 and Med27.
###end p 50

###xml 301 302 301 302 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 296 302 296 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med15<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 322 330 322 330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 381 382 381 382 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

###xml 943 944 927 928 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 951 952 935 936 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

###xml 962 963 946 947 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 957 963 941 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med31<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 965 967 949 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 968 970 952 954 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 1024 1048 1008 1024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50, &#916;med18</italic>
###xml 1053 1063 1029 1035 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 1115 1116 1087 1088 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1111 1116 1083 1088 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1127 1136 1099 1108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sep15-598</italic>
###xml 1142 1152 1114 1120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med27</italic>
###xml 1257 1265 1213 1221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1319 1320 1275 1276 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
