###xml 1397 1399 1353 1355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 1421 1431 1377 1383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 1609 1614 1561 1566 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50 B51 B52">50&#8211;52</xref>
###xml 1711 1712 1663 1664 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1707 1712 1659 1664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 2053 2062 1993 2002 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 3.</label>
###xml 2076 2084 2016 2024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 2104 2105 2044 2045 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 2402 2411 2336 2341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;ace2</italic>
###xml 2416 2425 2346 2351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;sep1</italic>
###xml 2456 2457 2382 2383 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 2062 2547 2002 2473 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="53">Phenotypes of <italic>S. pombe</italic> Mediator mutants. ###xml 2062 2547 2002 2473 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="53">Phenotypes of <italic>S. pombe</italic> Mediator mutants. ###xml 2547 2547 2473 2473 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkn070f3"/>
###xml 2053 2547 1993 2473 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F3" position="float"><label>Figure 3.</label><caption><p textid="53">Phenotypes of <italic>S. pombe</italic> Mediator mutants. (<bold>B</bold>) Ten-fold serial dilutions of wild-type and mutant cells under different forms of stress.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkn070f3"/></fig>
###xml 322 330 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 593 598 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 2076 2084 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
To discern functional subdivisions among Mediator subunits, we investigated the phenotypes of null alleles of med1+, med12+, med18+, med20+, med27+, med31+ as well as the SPBC146.01 gene encoding the proposed MED15 homolog. Deletion of med15+ in a diploid followed by tetrad analysis showed that med15+ is nonessential in S. pombe. We included the dead-kinase mutant allele of cdk8+ called ckd8mut (11) as well as med8ts (42) and med17Delta50. All mutants displayed one of two specific cellular morphologies-flocculation or hyphal growth (Figure 3A). Flocculation signifies the aggregation of yeast cells into larger clumps (47) and has previously been observed in Deltacdk8, Deltamed12 and Deltamed13 cells (10,48). Hyphal growth occurs when cells are unable to cleave the primary septum that separates two daughter cells following medial septation at the end of mitosis (49). This phenotype had previously been observed in ts alleles of med8+, med18+ and med31+ (41,44). The cellular morphology of the head domain mutants med17Delta50, Deltamed18 and Deltamed20 corresponded to the hyphal growth seen for the med8+ ts allele sep15-598. The Deltamed27 mutant did not have a visible phenotype at 30degreesC, but showed some septation defects at 37degreesC (Figure 3A). A complete deletion of middle domain subunit med31+ also displayed a hyphal growth phenotype in agreement with previous report (41). Interestingly, the Deltamed15 mutant also showed this phenotype. We included the two null mutants of G2/M transcription factors Ace2 and Sep1 for comparison, both of which display a severe septation defect (50-52). The Cdk8 module mutants flocculated, but showed no septation defects. Mutants lacking the med1+ gene did not have a visible phenotype at 30degreesC, but flocculated at 37degreesC. In summary, we observed a clear distinction in cellular morphology between Cdk8 module mutants (and the associated middle domain subunit Med1) and those of the head domain as well as of middle domain subunit Med31 and the potential Mediator subunit Med15. Figure 3.Phenotypes of S. pombe Mediator mutants. (A) Light microscopy of wild-type and mutant cells cultured in YES medium grown at 30degreesC unless otherwise indicated. Mediator mutants are organized according to their location within the Mediator. Unresolved septa are indicated by white arrows. The two well-characterized hyphal growth mutants Deltaace2 and Deltasep1 are included for comparison. (B) Ten-fold serial dilutions of wild-type and mutant cells under different forms of stress.
###end p 52

###xml 14 22 14 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>

###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 99 109 99 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 114 124 110 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med31</italic>
###xml 235 243 227 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 259 268 251 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;ace2</italic>
###xml 273 282 261 266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;sep1</italic>
###xml 421 431 399 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med27</italic>
###xml 524 534 498 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 683 685 653 655 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 679 711 649 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>ts</sup>, med17&#916;50, &#916;med18</italic>
###xml 725 746 687 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18 &#916;med20</italic>
###xml 826 836 780 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 853 863 803 809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 914 924 860 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med31</italic>
###xml 929 939 871 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 965 974 903 908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;ace2</italic>
###xml 979 988 913 918 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;sep1</italic>
We observed varying degrees of severity in the hyphal growth phenotype in the head domain mutants, Deltamed15 and Deltamed31. A spot assay was carried out to further discern the magnitude of growth inhibition in the septating mutants (Figure 3B). We included Deltaace2 and Deltasep1 for comparison. Cells were challenged with elevated temperatures (37degreesC), high salt (750 mM KCl) and 1% formamide, respectively. The Deltamed27 mutant appeared nearly indistinguishable from wild-type cells at all conditions tested. The Deltamed20 mutant was slightly more sensitive than wild type at high salt, but was very sensitive to heat and formamide. The remaining head domain mutants med8ts, med17Delta50, Deltamed18 as well as a Deltamed18 Deltamed20 double mutant grow very poorly at all conditions tested. Thus, in these assays Deltamed18 is epistatic to Deltamed20. Equal degree of sensitivity was observed for the Deltamed31 and Deltamed15 mutants. The two mutants Deltaace2 and Deltasep1 were indistinguishable from wild type indicating that it was not the hyphal growth defect in itself that caused slow growth and stress sensitivity in the Mediator mutants. The Cdk8 module mutants were indistinguishable from wild type under all conditions tested (data not shown).
###end p 54
###begin title 55
Expression profiling of Mediator mutants
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 252 260 252 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 459 461 459 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 252 260 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
We asked whether the distinct morphological phenotypes of Mediator mutants reflected distinct effects on global gene transcription. Hence, we performed expression profiling on six mutant alleles that we considered a representative cross section of the S. pombe Mediator. Global expression profiles of mutant alleles in conjunction with hierarchal clustering analysis can be used in an analogous way to phenotypes as a way to discern functional relationships (53).
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 136 139 136 139 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mut</sup>

###xml 149 159 149 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med12</italic>
###xml 168 178 164 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 188 198 180 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>

Error bars indicate 1 SD. (<bold>D</bold>) Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of SPBC1289.14 levels as described in (C).</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkn070f4"/></fig>
###xml 582 590 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
We made two sets of comparisons. The first set of comparisons consisted of three independent cultures of each of the mutant strains cdk8mut (TP274), Deltamed12 (TP27), Deltamed15 (TP130), Deltamed18 (TP126) and Deltamed20 (TP234) as well as a wild-type (MP9) control. The second set of comparisons consisted of two independent med17Delta50 cultures (TP392) with two wild-type (MP1) controls. We employed the Affymetrix platform and the number of genes changing in each mutant by a defined ratio threshold is shown in Figure 4B. Figure 4.Genome-wide expression analysis of nonlethal S. pombe Mediator alleles. (A) Heatmap cluster diagram of the 893 transcripts that change 2-fold or more in at least one of the mutants. Experiments and genes were hierarchically clustered according to average Pearson correlation linkage. The robustness of the experimental dataset clusters were analyzed by bootstrap analysis in MeV using 10 000 replicates. Numbers on branches indicate the range of bootstrap values expressed as percentages. (B) Bar diagram showing the number of genes changing 2-fold or more (yellow bars) and 10-fold or more (red bars) in each mutant strain. (C) Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of SPAC4H3.08 transcript levels of the mutant strains indicated as compared to wild-type cells. SPAC4H3.08 levels were normalized to 28 S rRNA. Error bars indicate 1 SD. (D) Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of SPBC1289.14 levels as described in (C).
###end p 57

###begin p 59
###xml 36 38 36 38 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B54">54</xref>
###xml 316 324 316 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 402 412 402 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 460 468 456 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 521 534 517 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 545 547 541 543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 875 883 871 879 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 521 534 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
We performed hierarchal clustering (54) on all genes changing 2-fold or more in the mutant datasets. The robustness of the clustering was tested by bootstrap analysis of 10 000 replicates with re-sampling of genes. The Cdk8 module mutants were clearly separated from the head domain subunits Med17, Med18 and Med20 (Figure 4A) as illustrated by the 100% bootstrap support of the Cdk8 module clade. The Deltamed15 mutant clustered within the head domain clade (Figure 4A), which is in agreement with previous results from S. cerevisiae Mediator (53). The genes that did change 2-fold or more belonged to diverse set of functional groups with no particular group of genes dominating any one expression profile-a reflection of the central role of Mediator in all pol II-dependent transcription. In addition, despite the significant correlation between expression profiles shown Figure 4A, each profile contained a set of genes particular to each mutant that showed a 2-fold or more change in transcript levels-in total 531 genes.
###end p 59

10<sup>&#8722;35</sup>)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>&#916;med20</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">2</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">68</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">24 (<italic>p</italic> = 1.4 &#215; ###xml 24 37 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 186 194 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 264 272 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Expression profiling of S. cerevisiae Mediator mutants have reported the increase of stress response gene transcript levels (46,53,55). We investigated whether this is also the case for S. pombe Mediator mutants. The central enviromental stress response (CESR) in S. pombe consists of a set of genes whose transcript levels consistently increase or decrease during various forms of stress (38). The Affymetrix array platform used in our study contained 134 of the induced CESR genes. We studied the occurrence of CESR genes above a defined fold change threshold and then calculated P-values using the hypergeometric probability distribution. We applied a 2-fold ratio change threshold for the cdk8mut, Deltamed12, Deltamed18 and Deltamed20 datasets, while the large number of genes changing in the Deltamed15 and med17Delta50 datasets required us to apply a 3-fold threshold in order to allow computation. The induced set of CESR genes were significantly overrepresented in the genes increasing their transcript levels above the threshold in all six datasets (Table 2, P < 0.001). In some mutants we also observed a significant overlap between downregulated genes and the genes belonging to the repressed set of CESR genes (data not shown). We confirmed the elevated transcription levels of the two induced CESR genes SPAC4H3.08 and SPBC1289.14 by quantitative real-time PCR analysis (Figure 4C and D). These genes are known to become induced 10-fold or more following heat shock and hydrogen peroxide treatment, respectively (38). Although all strains tested showed at least a 2-fold increase in transcript levels, a substantially higher degree of upregulation of these two genes were observed in the Deltamed15 mutant closely followed by the Deltamed18 mutant. These observations taken together suggest a central role for Mediator in the regulation of some CESR genes. The actual molecular mechanism of this regulation remains to be elucidated. ###end p 61

###xml 49 57 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 826 834 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1376 1384 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1508 1521 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1573 1586 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1737 1745 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1750 1763 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
We looked specifically at genes annotated in the S. pombe genome database as being involved in cell wall metabolism to explain the clear morphological differences between mutants of the Cdk8 module and those of the core Mediator. Specifically, we investigated genes known or proposed to be involved in the process of cell-to-cell adhesion as well as postmitotic septum dissolution. We could discern two major groups of genes with distinct expression patterns. The first group consisted of a family of genes that code for putative cell surface adhesins (56). These adhesins displayed increased transcript levels in the cdk8mut and Deltamed12 strains, but were largely unchanged in the head domain mutants (Figure 5A, orange bar). The increased transcript levels of these genes agree with the flocculation phenotype observed in S. pombe Cdk8 module mutants (Figure 3A) (10,48). The majority of the adhesin genes displayed only moderate increases in transcript levels (between 2- and 5-fold). One adhesin however, the DIPSY domain-containing SPAC186.01 gene, was upregulated nearly a 100-fold in the cdk8mut strain as assayed by quantitative real-time PCR (Figure 5B). This corresponded well with the stronger flocculation phenotype in this strain as compared to the somewhat milder phenotype observed for the Deltamed12 mutant (data not shown). Some of the other members of the S. pombe adhesin family that displayed more moderate increases in transcript levels are related to the FLO1, FLO5 and FLO9 genes of S. cerevisiae (56). The FLO genes are known to be upregulated in S. cerevisiae Cdk8 module mutants as well (46,53,55) and we conclude that the role of the Cdk8 module as a repressor of Flo-like adhesins appears conserved between S. pombe and S. cerevisiae. Figure 5.Mediator mutations affect genes involved in cell wall organization and metabolism. (A) Expression profiles of genes involved in cell wall metabolism, cell-to-cell adhesion and degradation of the post-mitotic primary septum. The first group (orange bar) includes cell surface proteins proposed to be involved in cell-to-cell adhesion during stress. The second group (green bar) includes genes previously known to cause hyphal growth when deleted. The corresponding datasets from previously described studies of other Mediator mutants (16) as well as null alleles of ace2+ and sep1+ (37) are included for comparison. (B) Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of SPAC186.01 transcript levels of the indicated mutant strains as compared to wild-type cells. SPAC186.01 levels were normalized to 28 S rRNA. Error bars indicate 1 SD. (C) Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of eng1+ levels as described in (B).
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 84 85 84 85 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>

###xml 569 570 569 570 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 565 570 565 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ace2<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 579 580 579 580 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

###xml 826 827 826 827 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
###xml 872 873 872 873 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 868 873 868 873 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eng1<sup>+</sup></italic>
Mediator mutations affect genes involved in cell wall organization and metabolism. (A) Expression profiles of genes involved in cell wall metabolism, cell-to-cell adhesion and degradation of the post-mitotic primary septum. The first group (orange bar) includes cell surface proteins proposed to be involved in cell-to-cell adhesion during stress. The second group (green bar) includes genes previously known to cause hyphal growth when deleted. The corresponding datasets from previously described studies of other Mediator mutants (16) as well as null alleles of ace2+ and sep1+ (37) are included for comparison. (B) Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of SPAC186.01 transcript levels of the indicated mutant strains as compared to wild-type cells. SPAC186.01 levels were normalized to 28 S rRNA. Error bars indicate 1 SD. (C) Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of eng1+ levels as described in (B).
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 18 26 18 26 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 119 129 119 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 298 299 294 295 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 294 299 290 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ace2<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 308 310 304 306 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 311 313 307 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 314 316 310 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 463 465 459 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 466 468 462 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 577 578 573 574 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 573 578 569 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ace2<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 591 593 587 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 594 596 590 592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 656 657 652 653 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 652 657 648 653 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sep1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 773 774 769 770 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 769 774 765 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ace2<sup>+</sup></italic>
The second group (Figure 5A, green bar) consisted of genes whose transcript levels were significantly decreased in the Deltamed15 and head domain mutants, but with no significant change in the Cdk8 module mutants. This group included genes regulated by the transcription factor Ace2 as well as ace2+ itself (37,51,57). These genes are expressed late in the cell cycle and involved the dissolution of the primary septum separating the newly formed daughter cells (51,57). Cells lacking these genes display septation defects. The Sep1 forkhead transcription factor regulates ace2+ expression (37,57). Sep1 precedes Ace2 in the regulatory pathway and the sep1+ gene was not affected by any of the mutants tested, suggesting that Sep1 requires the head domain subunits for ace2+ transcription.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 75 76 75 76 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 71 76 71 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 86 87 86 87 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 81 87 81 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med31<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 89 91 89 91 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 212 221 212 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;ace2</italic>
###xml 226 235 222 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;sep1</italic>
###xml 253 255 245 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 435 436 427 428 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 431 436 423 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ace2<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 451 452 443 444 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 447 452 439 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eng1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 637 646 629 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;ace2</italic>
###xml 651 660 639 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;sep1</italic>
###xml 668 670 652 654 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 729 730 713 714 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 725 730 709 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eng1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 781 790 765 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;ace2</italic>
###xml 795 804 775 780 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;sep1</italic>
###xml 945 955 921 927 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 986 995 958 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;ace2</italic>
###xml 1000 1009 968 973 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;sep1</italic>
###xml 1019 1027 983 991 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 1062 1070 1026 1034 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1158 1159 1122 1123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1154 1159 1118 1123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ace2<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1164 1165 1128 1129 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1160 1165 1124 1129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sep1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1062 1070 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
We also compared our profiles with published datasets of ts alleles of med8+ and med31+ (36). In agreement with their hyphal phenotypes only the Ace2-regulated genes were affected in these two mutants. Likewise, Deltaace2 and Deltasep1 expression data (37) did not exhibit any significant changes in expression of surface adhesins indicating that the Cdk8 module does not play a role in the expression of Ace2-dependent genes. The ace2+-regulated eng1+ gene encodes an endoglucanase that is required for the dissolution of the primary division septum following mitosis, and its deletion leads to a septation phenotype similar to that of Deltaace2 and Deltasep1 cells (51). We performed quantitative real-time PCR analysis of eng1+ transcript levels in the Mediator mutants and the Deltaace2 and Deltasep1 strains to directly compare the magnitude of decrease in this particular gene. We observed that the decrease in the head domain mutants and Deltamed15 was equivalent to that of the Deltaace2 and Deltasep1 mutants (Figure 5C). We therefore conclude that the S. pombe Mediator head domain and Med15 subunit play a crucial role in the transcription of ace2+/sep1+-dependent genes. We would like to point out that this analysis was done on asynchronous cells and therefore does not reveal any potential effect on the timing of cell cycle-dependent expression patterns.
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 37 50 37 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>

###xml 273 275 273 275 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>

###xml 430 432 430 432 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B59">59</xref>
###xml 563 571 563 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 627 640 627 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 732 736 732 736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACE2</italic>
###xml 762 764 762 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 894 902 894 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 907 920 907 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 922 931 922 931 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 6.</label>
###xml 1020 1033 1020 1033 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1207 1211 1207 1211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TUB1</italic>
###xml 1251 1264 1251 1264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1283 1285 1283 1285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 931 1287 931 1287 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="69">The requirement of the Mediator head and tail domain for Ace2-dependent transcription in <italic>S. cerevisiae</italic>. ###xml 931 1287 931 1287 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="69">The requirement of the Mediator head and tail domain for Ace2-dependent transcription in <italic>S. cerevisiae</italic>. ###xml 1287 1287 1287 1287 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkn070f6"/>
###xml 922 1287 922 1287 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F6" position="float"><label>Figure 6.</label><caption><p textid="69">The requirement of the Mediator head and tail domain for Ace2-dependent transcription in <italic>S. cerevisiae</italic>. ###xml 37 50 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 106 114 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 251 259 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 376 389 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 627 640 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 894 902 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 907 920 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1020 1033 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1251 1264 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
Degradation of the primary septum in S. cerevisiae is controlled in part by the ACE2 gene, the homolog of S. pombe ace2+ (58,59). However, primary septum dissolution and cell separation is fundamentally different and most of the required factors lack S. pombe homologs (60,61). Nevertheless, quantitative real-time PCR analysis of three genes wholly or partially regulated by S. cerevisiae ACE2-AMN1/CTS13, DSE2 and DSE4/ENG1 (58,59) all displayed decreased transcript levels in head and tail domain mutants compared to wild-type cells when grown in rich medium (Figure 6). Analysis of previously published expression data for S. cerevisiae Mediator mutants grown in minimal media revealed that this effect can be observed in other ACE2-regulated genes as well (53). We therefore conclude that the requirement of the head and tail domain for Ace2-dependent expression appears conserved between S. pombe and S. cerevisiae. Figure 6.The requirement of the Mediator head and tail domain for Ace2-dependent transcription in S. cerevisiae. Quantitative real-time PCR analysis of transcript levels of the indicated mutant strains as compared to wild-type cells. Transcript levels for all genes were normalized to TUB1 in accordance with previous studies of S. cerevisiae Mediator mutants (53).
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 89 102 89 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 276 280 276 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TUB1</italic>
###xml 320 333 320 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 352 354 352 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 89 102 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 320 333 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
The requirement of the Mediator head and tail domain for Ace2-dependent transcription in S. cerevisiae. ###end p 69
###begin title 70
DISCUSSION
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 114 122 114 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 328 336 328 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 376 388 376 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 536 544 532 540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 114 122 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
In this study, we use a combined genetic and biochemical approach to perform a functional characterization of the S. pombe Mediator complex. Our data suggest a head module architecture with a stepwise structural organization: Med27 located on the very exterior connected to Med20, which in turn contacts Med18 which binds Med8 (Figure 1E). Biochemical characterization of the med17Delta50 allele suggested that Med17 may act as scaffold for the head domain subunits and this function requires an intact C-terminus of the Med17 subunit (Figure 2C and D).
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 107 115 107 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 132 142 132 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med27</italic>
###xml 205 213 201 209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 286 294 282 290 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 410 418 406 414 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 506 516 502 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 524 532 516 524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 570 578 562 570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 615 625 607 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 673 681 661 669 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 700 710 688 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 750 760 734 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 770 791 750 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18 &#916;med20</italic>
###xml 840 850 812 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 891 896 853 858 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med18</italic>
###xml 913 918 875 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med20</italic>
###xml 986 996 948 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 1007 1015 965 973 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1138 1148 1096 1102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med18</italic>
###xml 1150 1158 1104 1112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1169 1171 1123 1125 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ts</sup>
###xml 1165 1171 1119 1125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med8<sup>ts</sup></italic>
###xml 1179 1187 1133 1141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1201 1213 1155 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 1253 1261 1203 1211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1377 1387 1327 1333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 1476 1486 1422 1428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med20</italic>
###xml 1494 1502 1436 1444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
Removal of Med27 does not affect the association of Med18 or Med20 with Mediator to any detectable extent (Figure 1D). In addition, Deltamed27 cells do not display visible phenotypes unless heat stressed (Figure 3A) and appear only marginally less stress tolerant than wild-type cells (Figure 3B). Removal of Med20 also caused the complete loss of Med27 as well as an apparent decrease in the amount of Med18 (Figure 1C). A corresponding increase in severity is observed both in the cellular morphology of Deltamed20 cells (Figure 3A) as well as their stress tolerance (Figure 3B). The strongest effect was seen in Deltamed18 Mediator where both Med20 and Med27 were lost (Figure 1C). Similarly, the Deltamed18 phenotype was more severe than that of Deltamed20 cells. A Deltamed18 Deltamed20 double mutant appeared indistinguishable from a Deltamed18 strain at 30degreesC demonstrating that med18 is epistatic to med20. This is what we would expect as Med20 is unable to associate with Deltamed18 Mediator (Figure 1C). Consolidation of the biochemical data with the observed phenotypes indicated that the loss of Med18, which occurred in Deltamed18 (Figure 1C) and med8ts cells (Figure 1D) as well as med17Delta50 cells cultured above room temperature (Figure 2C), appeared sufficient to cause the septation defect and stress hypersensitivity. The somewhat milder phenotype in Deltamed20 cell may well be caused by a decrease in the number of Med18 containing Mediator in the Deltamed20 cells (Figure 1C) rather than the loss of the Med20 subunit in itself.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 138 151 138 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 153 155 153 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 156 158 156 158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 177 198 177 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 249 271 245 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae srb4-138</italic>
###xml 311 332 307 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 383 391 375 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srb4-138</italic>
###xml 479 481 471 473 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B62">62</xref>
###xml 573 581 565 573 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 583 591 575 583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 613 626 605 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 635 637 627 629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 661 674 653 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 797 799 789 791 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 838 859 830 847 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 931 939 919 927 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1049 1070 1037 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 1078 1086 1062 1070 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1143 1155 1127 1135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med17&#916;50</italic>
###xml 1283 1285 1263 1265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B63">63</xref>
###xml 138 151 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 177 185 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 249 262 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 311 319 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 573 581 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 613 626 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 661 674 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 838 846 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1049 1057 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
The Med17 subunit has played a key role in establishing the almost absolute requirement for Mediator in pol II-dependent transcription in S. cerevisiae (45,46). The conditional S. pombe med17Delta50 allele isolated in this study is different to the S. cerevisiae srb4-138 allele in several respects. First, the S. pombe med17Delta50 allele is a C-terminally truncated form while the srb4-138 allele has a number of single nucleotide substitutions along the entire coding region (62). Second, we do not see an equally rapid growth arrest at the nonpermissive temperature in S. pombe (Figure 2A) as reported in the S. cerevisiae mutant (45). The growth arrest in S. cerevisiae appears directly linked to the immediate cessation of pol II-dependent transcription as the Mediator complex comes apart (19). The effect on Mediator stability in S. pombe med17Delta50 is less clear-cut with an increase in severity at higher temperatures (Figure 2C and D). We also observed that transcription does not shut down globally at the nonpermissive temperature in S. pombe med17Delta50 cells (Figure 2B). In addition, global chromatin immunoprecipitation of med17Delta50 Mediator showed a clear pattern of genomic reorganization after heat shock rather than a global reduction of Mediator binding (63).
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 57 65 57 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 219 229 219 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 307 316 303 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 322 323 318 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4</xref>
###xml 57 65 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
In this work, we addressed the function of the potential S. pombe Mediator subunit Med15. Our data clearly demonstrate a functional link between Med15 and Mediator. Specifically, the phenotype and transcript profile of Deltamed15 cells links Med15 to the head domain and to the middle domain subunit Med31 (Figures 3A and 4A). Presently, we do not know whether Med15 is able to stably associate with Mediator.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 676 689 676 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 796 798 796 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64">64</xref>
###xml 676 689 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
A relatively large number of core environmental stress-related (CESR) transcripts changed significantly in the expression profiles of all six Mediator mutants analyzed in this study. We interpret these data as the result of either one of two scenarios. First, the mutation might perturb cellular homeostasis to such a degree that the stress response is triggered as a secondary effect of the respective mutation. Alternatively, Mediator components could act as direct regulators of the stress response and so by removal of the regulator, the transcriptional program is triggered inadvertently. Further work will be required to shed light on this observation. However, Cdk8 in S. cerevisiae is known to specifically phosphorylate transcription factors directly involved in stress gene regulation (64), which therefore also would implicate Mediator as a direct regulator of the cellular stress response.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 147 155 147 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 174 183 174 183 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 189 190 189 190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5</xref>
###xml 312 320 312 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 435 437 435 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B47">47</xref>
###xml 473 486 473 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 515 517 515 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 518 520 518 520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B65">65</xref>
###xml 521 523 521 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B66">66</xref>
###xml 586 594 586 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 599 612 599 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 647 660 647 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 682 692 682 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FLO1, FLO5</italic>
###xml 697 701 697 701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FLO9</italic>
###xml 753 755 753 755 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 756 758 756 758 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B67">67</xref>
###xml 147 155 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 359 364 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 473 486 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 586 594 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 599 612 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 647 660 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
Expression profiles of genes known to be involved in cell wall metabolism correlated very well with the aberrant cellular morphologies observed in S. pombe Mediator mutants (Figures 3A and 5A-C). The flocculation phenotype seen in Cdk8 module mutants was likely the result of overproduction of surface adhesins (Figure 5A and B), a typical stress response in yeast and regulated by stress-related pathways such as MAP kinase cascades (47). Deletion of Cdk8 module genes in S. cerevisiae also leads to flocculation (46,65,66), suggesting that regulation of adhesins is conserved between S. pombe and S. cerevisiae. Indeed, transcript levels of the S. cerevisiae adhesin-coding genes FLO1, FLO5 and FLO9 are significantly elevated in Cdk8 module mutants (53,67).
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 155 165 155 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;med15</italic>
###xml 423 431 419 427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 436 449 432 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 451 453 447 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49">49</xref>
###xml 454 456 450 452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B60">60</xref>
###xml 462 470 458 466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 572 574 565 567 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 585 598 578 591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 695 697 688 690 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 836 844 829 837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 930 932 919 921 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B68">68</xref>
###xml 938 951 927 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1030 1032 1016 1018 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 1033 1035 1019 1021 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B69">69</xref>
###xml 1177 1185 1163 1171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1190 1203 1176 1189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1321 1329 1307 1315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1399 1407 1385 1393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1412 1425 1398 1411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1471 1480 1457 1466 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figures 5</xref>
###xml 1486 1487 1472 1473 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6</xref>
###xml 1490 1492 1476 1478 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 1543 1551 1529 1537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 423 431 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 436 449 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 462 470 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 585 598 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 836 844 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 938 951 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1177 1185 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1190 1203 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1321 1329 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1399 1407 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1412 1425 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1543 1551 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Conversely, the decreased expression of genes involved in the degradation of primary septum would explain the hyphal growth in head domain mutants and the Deltamed15 strain. Although transcription was not completely abolished the cumulative effect of several downregulated genes might gives rise to the hyphal growth. The process of septum dissolution to achieve complete cell separation is fundamentally different between S. pombe and S. cerevisiae (49,60). In S. pombe the primary septum consists of 1,3-beta-glucan which is primarily degraded by the Eng1 endoglucanse (51) while in S. cerevisiae the primary septum is made up of chitin and is subsequently degraded by the Cts1 endochitinase (51). The cell wall material surrounding the septum, the so-called septum edging, also differs in its composition between the two species. In S. pombe it is mainly composed of 1,3-alpha-glucan that is degraded by the Agn1 endoglucanse (68). In S. cerevisiae, the septum edging is 1,3-beta-glucan and degraded by the Eng1 endo-glucanse (61,69). The process is regulated by the conserved Ace2 transcription factor in both species but most of the target genes are not conserved between S. pombe and S. cerevisiae. We were therefore quite struck by the fact that the Mediator head domain and tail domain (only the Med15 subunit in S. pombe) were required for proper expression of Ace2-dependent genes in both S. pombe and S. cerevisiae despite the many differences in the process (Figures 5A and 6) (53). Even though the tail domain is not conserved in S. pombe, the Med15 protein still has an essential role to play in the Ace2-regulated septation cascade.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 82 90 82 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 178 186 178 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 205 213 205 213 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 941 942 941 942 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 937 942 937 942 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ace2<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1060 1068 1060 1068 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1153 1162 1153 1162 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 7.</label>
###xml 1245 1253 1245 1253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1305 1307 1305 1307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 1162 1852 1162 1852 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="79">Two classes of nonessential mutant alleles in fission yeast Mediator. A diagram of <italic>S. pombe</italic> L-Mediator based on single-particle EM structures (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>). The functional data presented in this work allow us to draw a virtual line through the Mediator. To the left are components of the Cdk8 module and the middle domain subunit Med1. When deleted these cells aggregate due to the overexpression of adhesive surface proteins as outlined in the text. To the right are mutant alleles of the head domain as well as the nonessential middle domain subunit Med31 and the Med15 factor. These mutants have a hyphal growth defect due to the faulty expression of genes required for efficient cell separation.</p>
###xml 1162 1852 1162 1852 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="79">Two classes of nonessential mutant alleles in fission yeast Mediator. ###xml 1852 1852 1852 1852 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkn070f7"/>
###xml 1153 1852 1153 1852 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F7" position="float"><label>Figure 7.</label><caption><p textid="79">Two classes of nonessential mutant alleles in fission yeast Mediator. A diagram of <italic>S. pombe</italic> L-Mediator based on single-particle EM structures (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>). ###xml 82 90 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 178 186 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1060 1068 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1208 1221 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">fission yeast</span>
###xml 1245 1253 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
In summary, the data presented in this article suggest a structural model for the S. pombe head domain and clearly defines two distinct functional classes of subunits within the S. pombe Mediator complex (Figure 7). The first class consists of all four components of the Cdk8 module as well as middle domain subunit Med1. If deleted, this group all flocculate due to de-repression of cell surface adhesions, some of which may be involved in mating, stress response or adaptation to starvation conditions. The second class is composed of the head domain as well as middle domain subunit Med31 and the as yet unassigned Med15 protein. When mutated these genes cause septation defects leading to hyphal growth due to impaired expression of the Ace2-dependent genes involved in cell separation. Our results and previously published expression data indicate that the head domain, Med31 and Med15 are required for the proper expression of the ace2+ gene, possibly by the Sep1 transcription factor. Thus, our work identifies two distinct functional submodules of the S. pombe Mediator that have conserved roles in the regulation of specific cellular pathways. Figure 7.Two classes of nonessential mutant alleles in fission yeast Mediator. A diagram of S. pombe L-Mediator based on single-particle EM structures (11). The functional data presented in this work allow us to draw a virtual line through the Mediator. To the left are components of the Cdk8 module and the middle domain subunit Med1. When deleted these cells aggregate due to the overexpression of adhesive surface proteins as outlined in the text. To the right are mutant alleles of the head domain as well as the nonessential middle domain subunit Med31 and the Med15 factor. These mutants have a hyphal growth defect due to the faulty expression of genes required for efficient cell separation.
###end p 78
